package com.weeklycommit.domain.entity;

import jakarta.persistence.Column;
import jakarta.persistence.Entity;
import jakarta.persistence.GeneratedValue;
import jakarta.persistence.GenerationType;
import jakarta.persistence.Id;
import jakarta.persistence.Table;
import java.time.Instant;
import java.time.LocalDate;
import java.util.UUID;

/**
 * Derived read-model: one row per active carry-forward commit, tracking
 * provenance and streak length.
 */
@Entity
@Table(name = "carry_forward_fact")
public class CarryForwardFact {

	@Id
	@GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.UUID)
	@Column(nullable = false, updatable = false)
	private UUID id;

	/** The current (target) commit in the chain. */
	@Column(name = "commit_id", nullable = false)
	private UUID commitId;

	/** The week in which the original (root) commit was created. */
	@Column(name = "source_week", nullable = false)
	private LocalDate sourceWeek;

	/** The week in which this commit currently lives. */
	@Column(name = "current_week", nullable = false)
	private LocalDate currentWeek;

	/** Number of consecutive weeks this work has been carried forward. */
	@Column(name = "streak_length", nullable = false)
	private int streakLength;

	@Column(name = "rcdo_node_id")
	private UUID rcdoNodeId;

	@Column(name = "chess_piece")
	private String chessPiece;

	@Column(name = "refreshed_at", nullable = false)
	private Instant refreshedAt = Instant.now();

	// ---- Getters / Setters -----------------------------------------------

	public UUID getId() {
		return id;
	}
	public void setId(UUID id) {
		this.id = id;
	}

	public UUID getCommitId() {
		return commitId;
	}
	public void setCommitId(UUID commitId) {
		this.commitId = commitId;
	}

	public LocalDate getSourceWeek() {
		return sourceWeek;
	}
	public void setSourceWeek(LocalDate sourceWeek) {
		this.sourceWeek = sourceWeek;
	}

	public LocalDate getCurrentWeek() {
		return currentWeek;
	}
	public void setCurrentWeek(LocalDate currentWeek) {
		this.currentWeek = currentWeek;
	}

	public int getStreakLength() {
		return streakLength;
	}
	public void setStreakLength(int streakLength) {
		this.streakLength = streakLength;
	}

	public UUID getRcdoNodeId() {
		return rcdoNodeId;
	}
	public void setRcdoNodeId(UUID rcdoNodeId) {
		this.rcdoNodeId = rcdoNodeId;
	}

	public String getChessPiece() {
		return chessPiece;
	}
	public void setChessPiece(String chessPiece) {
		this.chessPiece = chessPiece;
	}

	public Instant getRefreshedAt() {
		return refreshedAt;
	}
	public void setRefreshedAt(Instant refreshedAt) {
		this.refreshedAt = refreshedAt;
	}
}

-- =============================================================================
-- Weekly Commit Module — Initial Schema (V1)
-- All timestamps are stored as TIMESTAMPTZ (UTC).
-- Primary keys use gen_random_uuid() (PostgreSQL 13+).
-- =============================================================================

-- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
-- Organisation and team hierarchy
-- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

CREATE TABLE organization (
    id          UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    name        TEXT        NOT NULL,
    created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    updated_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE team (
    id              UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    organization_id UUID        NOT NULL REFERENCES organization (id),
    name            TEXT        NOT NULL,
    parent_team_id  UUID        REFERENCES team (id),
    created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE user_account (
    id                    UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    organization_id       UUID        NOT NULL REFERENCES organization (id),
    email                 TEXT        NOT NULL,
    display_name          TEXT        NOT NULL,
    home_team_id          UUID        REFERENCES team (id),
    role                  TEXT        NOT NULL DEFAULT 'IC',
    weekly_capacity_points SMALLINT   NOT NULL DEFAULT 10,
    active                BOOLEAN     NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
    created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    updated_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    CONSTRAINT uq_user_org_email UNIQUE (organization_id, email)
);

CREATE TABLE team_membership (
    id         UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    team_id    UUID        NOT NULL REFERENCES team (id),
    user_id    UUID        NOT NULL REFERENCES user_account (id),
    role       TEXT        NOT NULL DEFAULT 'MEMBER',
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    CONSTRAINT uq_team_membership UNIQUE (team_id, user_id)
);

-- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
-- RCDO hierarchy
-- ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

CREATE TABLE rcdo_node (
    id            UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    node_type     TEXT        NOT NULL
                              CHECK (node_type IN ('RALLY_CRY', 'DEFINING_OBJECTIVE', 'OUTCOME')),
    status        TEXT        NOT NULL DEFAULT 'DRAFT'
                              CHECK (status IN ('DRAFT', 'ACTIVE', 'ARCHIVED')),
    parent_id     UUID        REFERENCES rcdo_node (id),
    title         TEXT        NOT NULL,
    description   TEXT,
    owner_team_id UUID        REFERENCES team (id),
    owner_user_id UUID        REFERENCES user_account (id),
    created_at    TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
    updated_at    TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE TABLE rcdo_change_log (
    id                UUID        PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    rcdo_node_id      UUID        NOT NULL REFERENCES rcdo_node (id),
    changed_by_user_id UUID       NOT NULL REFERENCES user_account (id),
    change_summary    TEXT        NOT NULL,
    previous_value    JSONB,
    new_value         JSONB,
    created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

## 80. assistant
OK. Now I've read enough to give you a real answer.

---

## My previous advice was calibrated for "ship well." SOTA is a different game.

If you're genuinely going for state-of-the-art in AI-augmented planning intelligence, then yes — several things I dismissed become necessary. But the other LLM's advice is still wrong about *how* and *when*. Let me be precise about what changes.

### What I was right about

**Your domain model is already unusually strong.** Immutable snapshots, append-only scope changes, carry-forward lineage with streak tracking, per-user per-week fact tables, RCDO hierarchy — this is legitimately better temporal data modeling than most production systems. That advantage doesn't change.

**The guardrails and evidence-grounding principles are correct regardless.** SQL stays authoritative, predictions are labeled as predictions, every answer traces to sources. These aren't pragmatic shortcuts — they're what separates SOTA from a demo.

### What I was wrong about

Here's where SOTA changes the calculus:

**1. A graph query layer IS needed — but not Neo4j.**

For SOTA, you need to answer multi-hop provenance questions like:
- "Trace the causal chain from ticket TKT-882 being blocked → carry-forward of commit C-281 across 3 weeks → RCDO branch starvation → manager exception escalation"
- "Which team members share blocker dependencies through linked tickets?"
- "What is the shortest path between this RCDO branch being under-invested and a specific carry-forward pattern?"

Recursive CTEs can handle individual chains. But composing across 4-5 heterogeneous edge types with path weighting and variable-length traversal gets genuinely ugly in SQL. For a research-grade system, you need a real graph query language.

**However**: the right call isn't adding Neo4j as a separate database. It's adding **Apache AGE** — a Postgres extension that gives you Cypher/openCypher queries on top of your existing Postgres. Same database, same transactions, no sync problem, no new deployment.

```sql
-- Apache AGE: multi-hop provenance in your existing Postgres
SELECT * FROM cypher('planning_graph', $$
  MATCH path = (t:Ticket {id: 'TKT-882'})-[:BLOCKED]->(c:Commit)
    -[:CARRIED_FORWARD*1..5]->(cf:Commit)
    -[:MAPS_TO]->(r:RcdoNode)
  RETURN path, length(path) as hops
  ORDER BY hops
$$) AS (path agtype, hops agtype);
```

You still have one database. The graph is a **view** over your SQL tables, not a separate store. But you get real graph traversal semantics for complex provenance questions.

**2. GraphRAG community detection IS useful — but not for what they said.**

The other LLM said "BYOG with your entities." That's backwards. Your organizational structure (teams, RCDOs) is already known — Leiden clustering over explicit hierarchy is pointless.

Where GraphRAG community detection actually earns its place for SOTA is on **emergent behavioral patterns**:

- Build a graph where nodes are commits/tickets and edges are weighted by co-carry-forward, shared-blocker, and same-RCDO-branch relationships
- Run community detection on *that*
- Discover clusters like "these 12 commits across 3 teams keep getting stuck together because of a shared infrastructure dependency that nobody has named"

That's a genuine insight that no amount of SQL aggregation or flat RAG retrieval can produce. The communities are behavioral, not organizational — the system discovers structure that humans haven't explicitly modeled.

For SOTA, you'd run this as a weekly batch job:
1. Export behavioral edges from SQL (co-carry-forward, shared blockers, scope-change correlation)
2. Run GraphRAG indexing with community detection
3. Generate community reports
4. Use Global Search for wide-scope pattern questions
5. Compare against your flat RAG baseline and **publish the delta**

That last step is the difference between "we use GraphRAG" and SOTA. You need ablation results.

**3. Python IS the right call for ML and evaluation.**

I was wrong to dismiss this as "fracturing the stack." For SOTA AI engineering, the Python ML ecosystem is not optional:

- **Model training**: scikit-learn / XGBoost for risk prediction models trained on your historical outcome data
- **Evaluation harness**: your `PromptEvalRunner.java` is good for schema validation, but SOTA eval needs RAGAS metrics, statistical significance testing, prompt sensitivity analysis, calibration curves
- **Feature engineering**: temporal feature computation with point-in-time correctness
- **GraphRAG SDK**: Microsoft's GraphRAG is Python-native

The clean boundary is:
- **Java monolith**: domain logic, API, workflow, real-time serving
- **Python service**: ML training, batch feature computation, evaluation harness, GraphRAG indexing

This isn't stack fragmentation — it's using the right tool for ML. Every serious AI-augmented system has this boundary.

**4. A feature store becomes necessary — but later.**

Feast is still premature *right now*. But for SOTA, the trajectory is:

1. **Now**: Your `UserWeekFact` / `CarryForwardFact` tables are your feature tables. Good.
2. **After training a model**: Add point-in-time join logic to your `ReadModelRefreshService` so you can reconstruct features as-of any historical timestamp
3. **When serving predictions online**: Then Feast (or equivalent) for guaranteed temporal correctness in online serving

The key feature engineering that your current schema supports but you're not exploiting:

```sql
-- Features your data model already supports for risk prediction
SELECT
  uwf.user_id,
  uwf.week_start,
  uwf.total_planned_points,
  uwf.total_achieved_points,
  uwf.carry_forward_count,
  uwf.scope_change_count,
  -- Lagged features (previous weeks)
  LAG(uwf.total_achieved_points, 1) OVER w AS prev_week_achieved,
  LAG(uwf.carry_forward_count, 1) OVER w AS prev_week_cf,
  LAG(uwf.carry_forward_count, 2) OVER w AS prev2_week_cf,
  -- Rolling averages
  AVG(uwf.total_achieved_points) OVER (PARTITION BY uwf.user_id
    ORDER BY uwf.week_start ROWS BETWEEN 4 PRECEDING AND 1 PRECEDING) AS avg_achieved_4w,
  -- Accuracy ratio
  CASE WHEN uwf.total_planned_points > 0
    THEN uwf.total_achieved_points::float / uwf.total_planned_points
    ELSE NULL END AS completion_ratio,
  -- Target: did this plan have carry-forwards?
  CASE WHEN uwf.carry_forward_count > 0 THEN 1 ELSE 0 END AS had_carry_forward
FROM user_week_fact uwf
WINDOW w AS (PARTITION BY uwf.user_id ORDER BY uwf.week_start)
ORDER BY uwf.user_id, uwf.week_start;
```

That query, run over your historical seed data, gives you a supervised learning dataset for carry-forward prediction. **Your existing schema already supports this.** What you're missing is the model training and evaluation pipeline — which is Python.

### What I'd still push back on

**pgvector replacing Pinecone**: For SOTA, this is a "nice to have" (colocation, no vendor dependency) but not a prerequisite. Your Pinecone integration works, your `ChunkBuilder` enrichment is already good. Migrating vector stores is engineering work with zero intelligence improvement. Do it eventually for architectural cleanliness, not for SOTA.

**NeoDash / Bloom**: Still wrong. Your React frontend is where the evidence UI belongs. A separate dashboard tool fragments the user experience. Build the provenance visualization as React components.

**"Two graphs" (operational + GraphRAG)**: The separation is right in principle but the other LLM made it sound like two separate database deployments. With Apache AGE + a weekly GraphRAG batch job, you get the same effect without the sync burden.

### What SOTA actually requires that neither of us mentioned

Here's what's really missing if you want this to be genuinely state-of-the-art:

**A. Ablation studies and baselines.**

SOTA means you can prove each layer adds measurable value. You need:

| Comparison | What it proves |
|---|---|
| Vector-only RAG vs SQL+Vector | Structured retrieval matters |
| SQL+Vector vs SQL+Vector+Graph | Graph provenance adds value |
| Rules-only risk vs Rules+LLM risk | LLM augmentation catches real risks |
| Flat RAG vs GraphRAG Global Search | Community-based synthesis is superior for wide-scope questions |
| Current prompts vs few-shot enriched prompts | Prompt engineering ROI |
| LLM risk prediction vs trained ML model | Whether a trained model outperforms prompted LLM |

Without these comparisons, published with results, you have a system that uses advanced techniques. With them, you have SOTA.

**B. Calibration and abstention.**

Your `RiskDetectionService` assigns risk signals but doesn't report confidence. A SOTA system needs:

- When the model says 0.82 confidence on a carry-forward prediction, it should be right ~82% of the time
- When evidence is insufficient, the system should **refuse to answer** rather than hallucinate
- Calibration curves plotted over time, showing the system improves

**C. Counterfactual simulation.**

The "What-If Planner" I mentioned before becomes central for SOTA:

Given a draft plan + historical features + graph context, simulate:
- "If I move this Queen to next week, how does team RCDO coverage change?"
- "If this blocker resolves by Wednesday, which carry-forward chain clears?"
- "What is the minimum-risk plan that covers all active Outcomes?"

This isn't prompt engineering. It's constraint optimization informed by ML features, with the LLM used only for explanation rendering.

**D. Temporal evaluation — replay on your own history.**

Your V11 rich demo seed has 12+ weeks of data across 6 users. For SOTA:

1. Train on weeks 1-8
2. Predict risk/carry-forward for weeks 9-12
3. Compare predictions against actual reconcile outcomes
4. Report precision, recall, F1, and calibration
5. Publish the results

That's a reproducible benchmark that proves the system learns from history.

### Revised architecture for SOTA

```

### The sequence that matters

SOTA isn't about having all the pieces — it's about proving each one works in order:

1. **Now**: `StructuredEvidenceService` in Java — combine SQL + Pinecone retrieval into typed evidence bundles. This is the foundation everything else builds on. Evidence drawer in React.

2. **Week 2-4**: Apache AGE for graph traversal. Publish first ablation: SQL+Vector vs SQL+Vector+Graph for provenance questions.

3. **Week 4-6**: Python ML service. Train carry-forward and risk prediction models on historical feature data. Publish calibration curves and comparison against rules-only baseline.

4. **Week 6-8**: GraphRAG batch indexer on behavioral edges. Publish comparison: flat RAG vs GraphRAG Global Search for wide-scope pattern questions.

5. **Week 8-10**: Counterfactual simulation engine. Temporal replay evaluation on historical seed data. Published benchmark results.

6. **Week 10-12**: Abstention logic, confidence calibration, full eval harness with all AI capabilities, `README.md` and `docs/architecture.md` with results.

### Bottom line, revised

My previous advice was: "the mental model is right, the stack is wrong, do it all in Postgres." For SOTA, the honest answer is:

- Apache AGE (not Neo4j) — yes, you need graph traversal
- GraphRAG on behavioral patterns (not organizational structure) — yes, for emergent insight discovery
- Python ML service — yes, for model training, evaluation, and batch processing
- Feature store — yes, but after you train your first model
- Ablation studies and published benchmarks — this is what actually makes it SOTA

The differentiator between "good AI system" and SOTA isn't the number of technologies. It's **whether you can prove each layer adds measurable value over the one below it, with reproducible evaluation on your own data.**

That's the bar. And your data model is genuinely good enough to clear it.

## 83. toolResult
Weekly Commit Module

active
Category:

ai-accelerated
Role:

All Roles
Problem Statement

The organization currently uses 15-Five for weekly planning, but it has no structural connection between individual weekly commitments and organizational strategic goals. Managers lack visibility into how team members' weekly work maps to Rally Cries, Defining Objectives, and Outcomes, making it impossible to identify misalignment until it's too late. The challenge is to build a production-ready micro-frontend module that replaces 15-Five with a system that enforces this connection through a complete weekly lifecycle: commit entry, prioritization, reconciliation, and manager review.

Functional Requirements

Weekly commit CRUD with RCDO hierarchy linking, chess layer for categorization and prioritization, full weekly lifecycle state machine (DRAFT → LOCKED → RECONCILING → RECONCILED → Carry Forward), reconciliation view comparing planned vs. actual, manager dashboard with team roll-up, micro-frontend integration into existing PA host app following the PM remote pattern

Required Languages

TypeScript (strict mode), Java 21, SQL

## 92. assistant
OK. Let me actually think about this.

---

## The honest answer: no, most of that SOTA plan doesn't make sense for this project.

I got carried away. The other LLM got carried away. Let me walk through why.

### What the assignment actually asks for

Re-reading `assignment.md`:

- **Category**: `ai-accelerated` — AI is a *quality* of the product, not the product itself
- **Problem**: Replace 15Five with structured weekly planning connected to strategy
- **Functional requirements**: Commit CRUD, RCDO linking, chess layer, lifecycle state machine, reconciliation, manager dashboard, micro-frontend
- **Required languages**: TypeScript (strict mode), Java 21, SQL

That's it. The assignment is a **planning workflow product** that happens to be AI-accelerated. It's not a research project. It's not a paper. It's not an ML platform.

### What you already have

241 Java source files. 95 TypeScript components. 54 backend tests. 41 frontend tests. 4 E2E specs. 13 Flyway migrations. 10 prompt templates. A RAG pipeline. Faithfulness evaluation. Prometheus metrics. CI on both GitHub Actions and GitLab CI. A 775-line demo seed.

This is already an extremely strong submission. Most people building this assignment don't have half of what you have.

### Why Apache AGE doesn't make sense

Let me be specific:

**Your graph is small and well-typed.** You have carry-forward links (source → target), RCDO hierarchy (parent → child), team membership, plan → commit → ticket. That's maybe 6 relationship types, all with explicit foreign keys. A recursive CTE handles any traversal you'd actually need.

Apache AGE would require:
- A non-standard Postgres extension (compile from source or specific Docker image)
- Maintaining a graph projection alongside your relational schema
- Learning and debugging openCypher
- Explaining to an evaluator why you added graph query infrastructure for what amounts to `WITH RECURSIVE`

The evaluator is going to look at your `CarryForwardService` with its lineage traversal and think "this person understands provenance." They're not going to dock points because you didn't use Cypher.

**The complexity cost is real, the intelligence gain is near-zero for this domain.**

### Why ablation studies don't make sense

Ablation studies prove that each component of a system contributes measurable value. They exist for research papers where reviewers need to be convinced.

Your evaluator is not a conference reviewer. They're looking at whether your AI features are:
1. Integrated into the workflow (not bolted on)
2. Explainable (rationale on every suggestion)
3. Auditable (stored, with feedback)
4. Gracefully degrading (system works without AI)
5. Actually useful

You already satisfy all five. Formal ablation would mean building multiple stripped-down variants of your system, running them against test data, computing metrics, and writing up results. That's weeks of work that produces a document, not a better product.

What WOULD be valuable — and is much cheaper — is completing your eval fixtures for all 6 AI capabilities and showing the results. That's "our AI is tested and we can prove it works," which is the assignment-appropriate version of what ablation tries to demonstrate.

### Why a Python ML service doesn't make sense

The assignment says **TypeScript, Java 21, SQL**. Adding Python:
- Introduces a language outside the requirements
- Adds a deployment boundary (a separate service with its own health checks, error handling, API)
- Requires explaining why the Java monolith that handles everything else can't handle this

For what? To train a carry-forward prediction model on your 775-line seed data? You don't have enough real historical data to train anything meaningful. Your rules-based `RiskDetectionService` with its 5 signal types + LLM augmentation is already the right architecture for this scale.

If you wanted a trained model eventually, Java has Tribuo (Oracle's ML library) and you could do logistic regression on your `UserWeekFact` features without leaving the JVM. But even that is unnecessary for this assignment.

### Why GraphRAG doesn't make sense

GraphRAG's community detection needs scale to produce meaningful clusters. Your demo seed has 6-8 users across 12 weeks. Leiden clustering on that graph would produce trivial or meaningless communities. The "emergent behavioral patterns" I described sound impressive but require hundreds of users over months of real data to be detectable.

Your existing `InsightGenerationService` — which gathers structured data, retrieves historical context from Pinecone, and synthesizes insights — is already doing the job GraphRAG would do, at the scale your data actually supports.

### What actually matters for making this outstanding

Here's what I think you should focus on, in priority order:

**1. Tell the story.**

You don't have a `README.md`. That means the first thing an evaluator sees is... a file listing. Your 241-class backend, 10 prompt templates, RAG pipeline, faithfulness evaluator — all invisible until someone digs.

A strong README with:
- What this is and why it matters
- Architecture diagram showing the AI pipeline
- Screenshot or GIF of the actual UI
- "How to run" (you already have `make dev`)
- What the AI does and how it's evaluated
- Demo personas and walkthrough

That single file probably moves the needle more than any infrastructure addition.

**2. Complete the evaluation story.**

You have eval fixtures for 2 of 6 AI capabilities (`commit-draft-assist`: 12 cases, `commit-lint`: 6 cases). The infrastructure is already built — `PromptEvalRunner`, `EvalCase`, `EvalResult`, the `evalTest` Gradle task, the GitLab CI stage. The hard part is done.

Adding fixtures for:
- `rcdo-suggest`
- `risk-signal`
- `reconcile-assist`
- `rag-query`

...and running `./gradlew evalTest` with real results is straightforward work that directly demonstrates AI engineering rigor. An evaluator seeing "we test all 6 AI capabilities against golden datasets with LLM-as-judge scoring" is genuinely impressive.

**3. Fix the doc drift.**

Your `docs/ai-eval-roadmap.md` references:
- `docs/rag-eval-research.md` — doesn't exist
- Frontend AI components as "MISSING" — but `CommitDraftAssistButton.tsx` and `ReconcileAssistPanel.tsx` exist
- `infra/grafana/provisioning/dashboards/ai-quality.json` — not present

This kind of drift makes an evaluator wonder if the docs are aspirational rather than real. Updating the roadmap to reflect what's actually built (and marking remaining items honestly) shows maturity.

**4. Build ONE impressive capability that demonstrates intelligence depth.**

Not five new infrastructure components. One feature that makes an evaluator think "oh, that's clever."

My vote: **the Structured Evidence Service.** Not because it requires new infrastructure, but because it changes the quality of AI answers from "here's what the LLM said based on some vector chunks" to "here are the SQL facts, here's the lineage chain, here's the semantic evidence, here's the risk assessment, and here's the LLM's synthesis of all of that."

This is achievable in your existing Java stack:

```java
public record StructuredEvidence(
    SqlFacts facts,           // from existing repositories
    LineageChain lineage,     // recursive CTE on carry_forward_link
    List<SemanticMatch> evidence,  // from existing Pinecone pipeline
    RiskFeatures features     // from existing UserWeekFact/CarryForwardFact
) {}
```

Wire it into `SemanticQueryService` so RAG answers are grounded in structured evidence, not just vector similarity. Show the evidence in the UI alongside the answer.

That's the "deeply intelligent" move — not because the technology is exotic, but because the system **reasons across structured and unstructured data and shows its work.** That's what the PRD's "explainable, auditable AI" principle actually looks like in practice.

**5. If you have time: the What-If feature.**

A single endpoint:

```
POST /api/ai/what-if
{
  "planId": "...",
  "hypotheticalChanges": [
    {"action": "ADD_COMMIT", "title": "...", "chessPiece": "QUEEN", "points": 5},
    {"action": "REMOVE_COMMIT", "commitId": "..."}
  ]
}
```

That computes capacity impact, RCDO coverage change, and risk delta — mostly from your existing rules engine and feature tables — and uses the LLM to narrate the implications. No new infrastructure. Just a smart composition of things you already have.

### Why I'm thinking this way

I went through three phases on this project:

1. **First look**: "This is solid but needs packaging and a few more capabilities"
2. **After the other LLM's response**: "OK, for SOTA you need graph databases and ML pipelines"
3. **After re-reading the assignment**: "Wait — what are we actually optimizing for?"

The answer is: you're optimizing for demonstrating that you can build a production-quality, AI-accelerated planning system with the specified tech stack. Not for publishing at a conference. Not for building an ML platform.

The things that make this outstanding in that context are:
- The AI is woven into the product workflow, not a sidebar chatbot
- Every suggestion is explainable, auditable, and dismissible
- The system works without AI (graceful degradation)
- The evaluation story is rigorous and complete
- The repo tells its own story clearly

You're 80% there. The remaining 20% is completion and narrative, not new infrastructure.

Adding Apache AGE, GraphRAG, a Python service, and Feast would likely produce a repo with impressive-sounding architecture and half-finished implementations — which is worse than the polished, complete system you have now. The evaluator will spend 30-60 minutes with this. A clean README, a working demo, complete eval results, and one "that's clever" feature will land harder than a sprawling architecture diagram with components that aren't fully wired.

Good question. Let me think about this against what would actually impress a company, not what sounds impressive on paper.

### What I'd take from the previous discussions

**The What-If Planner — yes, absolutely.** This is the single highest-impact beyond-scope feature. Here's why:

Every other AI feature in your system describes what *is* or what *was*. The What-If Planner is the only one that reasons about what *could be*. That's a qualitative leap. When an evaluator sees "if you add this 5-point Queen, you'll exceed capacity and RCDO branch X loses coverage — here's what to de-scope," they're seeing something that most AI-augmented products never attempt.

And it's buildable with what you have. Your `RiskDetectionService` already computes overcommit/undercommit/volatility. Your `UserWeekFact` and `RcdoWeekRollup` already have the historical features. You just need an endpoint that applies hypothetical mutations to a plan copy, runs the existing rules + feature lookups, and uses the LLM to narrate the implications. No new infrastructure.

**Historical replay benchmark — yes, in a lightweight form.** Not a formal ablation study, but: take your 12-week seed data, run your risk detection on weeks 1-8 as if they were current, and compare the predictions to what actually happened in weeks 9-12 (reconcile outcomes, carry-forwards, etc.). Publish the results as `docs/eval-results.md`. A company seeing "our carry-forward prediction achieves 71% precision on historical data" will understand this person takes AI engineering seriously.

### What I'd leave behind

**Apache AGE** — still no. Your carry-forward lineage is a linear chain. Your RCDO hierarchy is a tree. Both are trivially handled by recursive CTEs. AGE adds Postgres extension management complexity for zero perceptible intelligence gain. A company evaluator won't notice graph query syntax; they'll notice whether your lineage traversal works and is well-tested.

**GraphRAG** — no. You have 6-8 users across 12 weeks. Community detection on that data would produce noise, not insight. If you ever scale to hundreds of users with months of real data, revisit it. Not now.

**Python ML service** — no. The assignment specifies Java 21, TypeScript, SQL. Going outside the required languages to add a separate service is a risk signal ("does this person scope well?"), not a strength. If you want predictive scoring, do it in Java on your existing feature tables. A hand-tuned scoring function or even Tribuo (Oracle's Java ML library) would demonstrate the same thinking without the deployment complexity.

**Neo4j / Feast / NeoDash** — no. All of these are solutions looking for problems you don't have at this scale.

### What I think would genuinely stand out

Here's my proposed scope, in implementation order:

| # | Item | Why it impresses | Effort |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | `README.md` + `docs/architecture.md` | First thing anyone sees. Sets the narrative. | Small |
| 2 | Fix doc drift in `ai-eval-roadmap.md` | Shows the docs are alive, not aspirational | Small |
| 3 | Complete eval fixtures (4 remaining AI capabilities) + publish results | "We scientifically validate our AI" — most people never do this | Medium |
| 4 | `StructuredEvidenceService` + evidence in API responses | AI answers grounded in SQL facts + lineage + vector evidence + risk features, not just LLM output | Medium-Large |
| 5 | **What-If Planner** (beyond scope) | The system reasons about hypothetical futures | Medium |
| 6 | **Historical Replay Benchmark** (beyond scope) | Concrete proof the AI predictions work | Small-Medium |

Items 5 and 6 together tell a story no other submission will have: *"The system predicts what will happen, helps you decide what to change, and we can prove both work against real historical data."*

Want me to start executing on this? I'd begin with the README and architecture docs since they frame everything else, then work through the list in order.

## 116. toolResult
/**
 * Standalone app entry for local development.
 *
 * Includes a dev-only user switcher so you can demo as Manager, IC, or Admin
 * without restarting. The switcher is a fixed banner at the top of the page.
 */
import { useState } from "react";
import { BrowserRouter, Routes, Route, Navigate } from "react-router-dom";
import WeeklyCommitRoutes from "./Routes.js";
import { mockHostBridge, mockHostContext, defaultDesignTokens } from "./host/MockHostProvider.js";
import type { HostBridge } from "./host/HostProvider.js";

// ── Dev user roster — matches V9 + V11 seed UUIDs ──────────────────────────

interface DevUser {
  id: string;
  email: string;
  displayName: string;
  role: "MANAGER" | "IC";
  label: string;
}

const DEV_USERS: DevUser[] = [
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000001", email: "dev@example.com",     displayName: "Dev User",     role: "MANAGER", label: "Dev User (Manager)" },
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000002", email: "manager@example.com", displayName: "Manager One",  role: "MANAGER", label: "Manager One (Manager)" },
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000003", email: "alice@example.com",   displayName: "Alice Chen",   role: "IC",      label: "Alice Chen (IC)" },
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000004", email: "bob@example.com",     displayName: "Bob Martinez", role: "IC",      label: "Bob Martinez (IC)" },
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000005", email: "carol@example.com",   displayName: "Carol Nguyen", role: "IC",      label: "Carol Nguyen (IC)" },
  { id: "00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000006", email: "dan@example.com",     displayName: "Dan Okafor",   role: "IC",      label: "Dan Okafor (IC)" },
];

function buildBridge(user: DevUser): HostBridge {
  const isManager = user.role === "MANAGER";
  return {
    ...mockHostBridge,
    context: {
      ...mockHostContext,
      authenticatedUser: { id: user.id, email: user.email, displayName: user.displayName },
      featureFlags: {
        ...mockHostContext.featureFlags,
        managerReviewEnabled: isManager,
        rcdoAdminEnabled: isManager,
      },
    },
    tokens: defaultDesignTokens,
  };
}

// ── Dev switcher banner ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────

function DevUserSwitcher({ current, onChange }: { current: DevUser; onChange: (u: DevUser) => void }) {
  return (
    <div
      style={{
        position: "fixed", top: 0, left: 0, right: 0, zIndex: 9999,
        background: "#1a1a1a", color: "#e5e5e5",
        display: "flex", alignItems: "center", gap: "10px",
        padding: "4px 12px", fontSize: "11px", fontFamily: "monospace",
        borderBottom: "1px solid #333",
      }}
    >
      <span style={{ color: "#737373", flexShrink: 0 }}>👤 Dev user:</span>
      <select
        value={current.id}
        onChange={(e) => {
          const u = DEV_USERS.find((u) => u.id === e.target.value) ?? DEV_USERS[0]!;
          onChange(u);
        }}
        style={{
          background: "#2a2a2a", color: "#e5e5e5", border: "1px solid #444",
          borderRadius: "3px", padding: "2px 6px", fontSize: "11px",
          fontFamily: "monospace", cursor: "pointer",
        }}
      >
        {DEV_USERS.map((u) => (
          <option key={u.id} value={u.id}>{u.label}</option>
        ))}
      </select>
      <span style={{ color: "#555", marginLeft: "auto" }}>dev mode</span>
    </div>
  );
}

// ── App ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

export default function App() {
  // eslint-disable-next-line @typescript-eslint/no-non-null-assertion
  const [activeUser, setActiveUser] = useState<DevUser>(DEV_USERS[0]!);
  const bridge = buildBridge(activeUser);

  return (
    <>
      <DevUserSwitcher current={activeUser} onChange={setActiveUser} />
      {/* Push page content below the fixed switcher banner */}
      <div style={{ paddingTop: "28px" }}>
        <BrowserRouter>
          <Routes>
            <Route path="/" element={<Navigate to="/weekly" replace />} />
            <Route path="/weekly/*" element={<WeeklyCommitRoutes bridge={bridge} />} />
          </Routes>
        </BrowserRouter>
      </div>
    </>
  );
}

## 117. toolResult
/**
 * Route-level entry point exposed via Module Federation.
 * The PA host app imports this module to mount the weeklyCommit remote.
 *
 * Usage in host:
 *   const WeeklyCommitRoutes = React.lazy(() => import("weeklyCommit/Routes"));
 *   <WeeklyCommitRoutes bridge={hostBridge} />
 */
import { lazy, Suspense } from "react";
import { Routes, Route, Navigate } from "react-router-dom";
import { HostProvider, type HostBridge } from "./host/HostProvider.js";
import { AppShell } from "./components/AppShell.js";

const MyWeek = lazy(() => import("./routes/MyWeek.js"));
const Reconcile = lazy(() => import("./routes/Reconcile.js"));
const TeamWeek = lazy(() => import("./routes/TeamWeek.js"));
const Tickets = lazy(() => import("./routes/Tickets.js"));
const Rcdos = lazy(() => import("./routes/Rcdos.js"));
const Reports = lazy(() => import("./routes/Reports.js"));
const Admin = lazy(() => import("./routes/Admin.js"));

function RouteFallback() {
  return (
    <div
      role="status"
      aria-label="Loading page"
      className="py-8 text-center text-sm text-muted"
    >
      Loading…
    </div>
  );
}

interface WeeklyCommitRoutesProps {
  /** Host bridge injected by the PA host app. */
  readonly bridge: HostBridge;
}

/**
 * All weekly-commit routes wrapped in the HostProvider and AppShell.
 * The host must wrap this component with its own BrowserRouter (or
 * pass a MemoryRouter for integration tests).
 */
export default function WeeklyCommitRoutes({
  bridge,
}: WeeklyCommitRoutesProps) {
  return (
    <HostProvider bridge={bridge}>
      <AppShell>
        <Suspense fallback={<RouteFallback />}>
          <Routes>
            <Route index element={<Navigate to="my-week" replace />} />
            <Route path="my-week" element={<MyWeek />} />
            <Route path="reconcile" element={<Reconcile />} />
            <Route path="reconcile/:planId" element={<Reconcile />} />
            <Route path="team" element={<TeamWeek />} />
            <Route path="team/:teamId" element={<TeamWeek />} />
            <Route path="tickets" element={<Tickets />} />
            <Route path="rcdos" element={<Rcdos />} />
            <Route path="reports" element={<Reports />} />
            <Route path="admin" element={<Admin />} />
          </Routes>
        </Suspense>
      </AppShell>
    </HostProvider>
  );
}

Draft → Locked → Reconciling → Reconciled. |\n| **Commit** | A weekly work promise with title, chess piece, RCDO link, estimate points, success criteria. |\n| **RCDO Hierarchy** | Rally Cry → Defining Objective → Outcome. Every commit links to strategy. |\n| **Chess Layer** | King (must not fail) · Queen (highest leverage) · Rook · Bishop · Knight · Pawn. Max 1 King, 2 Queens per week. |\n| **Lock Snapshot** | Immutable baseline captured at lock. No silent edits — all post-lock changes are structured scope change events. |\n| **Reconciliation** | End-of-week comparison: planned vs actual, with carry-forward decisions. |\n| **Carry-Forward** | Explicit, with lineage. team/user/week)\n\nQuery Path:\n  Question → Intent Classification (entity types, time range, user scope)\n    → Embedding → Pinecone retrieval (top-40)\n    → Context assembly → Claude synthesis → Audited response with sources\n```\n\n### Evaluation Infrastructure\n\n- **Golden test datasets** for AI capabilities with automated + LLM-as-judge scoring\n- **FaithfulnessEvaluator** — async Evaluation Research (faithfulness < 0.88 → warning, < 0.85 → critical)\n- **Prompt version tracking** — every suggestion stores the prompt template version for A/B analysis\n\n---\n\n## Quick     "path": "docs/architecture.md",
    "content": "# Architecture\n\nThis document describes the technical architecture of the Weekly Commit Module. For product requirements, see [prd.md](prd.md). For AI evaluation infrastructure, see [ai-eval-roadmap.md](ai-eval-roadmap.md).\n\n---\n\n## System Overview\n\nThe Weekly Commit Module is a route-level micro-frontend integrated into the PA host app, backed by a Java 21 modular monolith. AI capabilities are woven into the domain workflow — not a separate layer — with graceful degradation if any AI dependency is unavailable.\n\n```\nBrowser → React MF Remote → REST/JSON → Spring Boot → PostgreSQL\n                                              │\n                                              ├──→ Pinecone (vector store)\n                                              ├──→ OpenRouter (LLM — Claude)\n                                              └──→ OpenAI (embeddings)\n```\n\n### Design Decisions\n\n| Decision | Rationale |\n|---|---|\n| **Modular monolith** over microservices | Complexity is in workflow and data integrity, not service decomposition. One DB transaction boundary keeps lock/reconcile snapshots consistent. |\n| **Derived read models** over live joins | Manager dashboards and RCDO rollups query pre-computed `*_fact` / `*_rollup` tables refreshed on lifecycle events + 5-minute cron. Meets P95 < 1.5s target. |\n| **AI behind provider abstraction** | `AiProvider` interface with `OpenRouterAiProvider` (production) and `StubAiProvider` (test/offline). Core workflow never depends on a single vendor. |\n| **Immutable snapshots** | Lock and reconcile each capture a snapshot (normalized rows + denormalized JSON). History cannot be rewritten — only appended to via scope change events. |\n| **Module Federation remote** | Frontend is a self-contained remote that receives host context (auth, design tokens, feature flags) via `HostProvider`. Runs standalone for dev with mock host bridge. |\n\n---\n\n## Backend Modules\n\nThe backend is organized as a package-per-bounded-context modular monolith:\n\n```\ncom.weeklycommit\n├── plan/           Weekly plan + commit CRUD, validation\n├── lock/           Lock service, auto-lock job, baseline snapshots\n├── reconcile/      Reconciliation, scope changes, outcome tracking\n├── carryforward/   Explicit carry-forward with lineage\n├── rcdo/           RCDO hierarchy management, linkage validation\n├── team/           Team weekly view, manager review, authorization\n├── ticket/         Native ticket/work item model, status workflow\n├── notification/   Rules-based notifications, email digest\n├── audit/          Audit logging for all lifecycle transitions\n├── config/         Org + team cadence configuration\n├── report/         Reporting service, read model refresh\n├── ai/             AI pipeline (see below)\n│   ├── controller/ Single REST controller for all AI endpoints\n│   ├── provider/   AiProvider abstraction, OpenRouter, Stub\n│   ├── service/    CommitDraftAssist, CommitLint, RcdoSuggest,\n│   │               RiskDetection, ReconcileAssist, ManagerSummary\n│   ├── rag/        Pinecone, Embedding, ChunkBuilder, SemanticQuery,\n│   │               SemanticIndex, InsightGeneration\n│   ├── eval/       FaithfulnessEvaluator (production scoring)\n│   ├── metrics/    Prometheus AI quality gauges\n│   └── dto/        Request/response records for all AI endpoints\n└── domain/\n    ├── entity/     33 JPA entities\n    ├── enums/      12 enum types\n    └── repository/ 33 Spring Data repositories\n```\n\n### API Surface\n\n13 REST controllers expose 60+ endpoints:\n\n| Controller | Prefix | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `PlanController` | `/api/plans` | Plan + commit CRUD, lock, reconcile |\n| `ReconcileController` | `/api/plans/{id}` | Scope changes, outcomes, reconcile submit |\n| `CarryForwardController` | `/api/plans/...` | Carry-forward with lineage |\n| `TeamController` | `/api/teams` | Team week view, exceptions, comments, capacity |\n| `TicketController` | `/api/tickets` | Ticket CRUD, status transitions, link to commits |\n| `RcdoController` | `/api/rcdo` | RCDO hierarchy CRUD, move, archive |\n| `AiController` | `/api/ai` | All AI endpoints (draft assist, lint, RAG, etc.) |\n| `ReportController` | `/api/reports` | 8 report types from derived read models |\n| `NotificationController` | `/api/notifications` | Notification list, mark read |\n| `AuditLogController` | `/api/audit-log` | Audit trail queries |\n| `ConfigController` | `/api/config` | Org + team cadence configuration |\n| `PlanHistoryController` | `/api/users` | Historical plan browsing |\n| `HealthController` | `/health` | Health check |\n\nFull OpenAPI spec available at `/api-docs` (JSON) and `/swagger-ui.html` (interactive).\n\n---\n\n## Data Model\n\n### Transactional Tables (source of truth)\n\n```\norganization ──< team ──< team_membership >── user_account\n                  │\n                  └──< weekly_plan ──< weekly_commit ──< carry_forward_link\n                              │              │\n                              │              ├── work_item (optional link)\n                              │              └── rcdo_node (required at lock)\n                              │\n                              ├──< lock_snapshot_header ──< lock_snapshot_commit\n                              ├──< reconcile_snapshot_header ──< reconcile_snapshot_commit\n                              ├──< scope_change_event\n                              └──< manager_comment\n\nrcdo_node (self-referencing tree) ──< rcdo_change_log\nwork_item ──< work_item_status_history\n              work_item_comment\n\nnotification ──< notification_delivery\nai_suggestion ──< ai_feedback\naudit_log\ncapacity_override\nmanager_review_exception\n```\n\n### Derived Read Models (refreshed, not source of truth)\n\n| Table | Grain | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `user_week_fact` | user × week | Points planned/achieved, compliance, carry-forward count, chess counts |\n| `team_week_rollup` | team × week | Member count, lock/reconcile counts, chess distribution (JSONB) |\n| `rcdo_week_rollup` | RCDO node × week | Points planned/achieved, team contribution breakdown (JSONB) |\n| `compliance_fact` | user × week | Lock on-time/late/auto, reconcile on-time/late/missed |\n| `carry_forward_fact` | commit | Source week, current week, streak length, RCDO, chess piece |\n\nRead models are refreshed by `ReadModelRefreshService`:\n- **Event-driven**: after lock, reconcile, scope change, carry-forward\n- **Scheduled**: every 5 minutes for the current week (catch-up sweep)\n- **Idempotent**: re-running with the same input produces the same result\n\n---\n\n## Weekly Lifecycle State Machine\n\n```\n                    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n                    │                                             │\n  Draft opens       ▼                                             │\n  ┌─────────┐   ┌──────┐   Lock    ┌────────┐   Reconcile   ┌────────────┐\n  │ (start) │──>│ DRAFT│──────────>│ LOCKED │──────────────>│RECONCILING │\n  └─────────┘   └──────┘           └────────┘   opens        └────────────┘\n                    │                  │                           │\n                    │ auto-lock        │ scope changes             │ submit\n                    │ at cutoff        │ (append-only events)      ▼\n                    └──────────────────┘                    ┌────────────┐\n                                                           │ RECONCILED │ (terminal)\n                                                           └────────────┘\n                                                                │\n                                                                │ carry-forward\n                                                                ▼\n                                                           New commit in\n                                                           next week's plan\n                                                           (with provenance)\n```\n\n**Key invariants:**\n- Lock creates an **immutable baseline snapshot** — the contract for the week\n- Post-lock edits create **scope change events** with required reason, not silent mutations\n- Reconcile creates an **immutable actual snapshot** with outcomes\n- Carry-forward creates a **new commit object** with `CarryForwardLink` — never mutates the original\n- Auto-lock at cutoff marks the plan as `system_locked_with_errors` (non-compliant)\n\n---\n\n## AI Pipeline\n\n### Provider Abstraction\n\n```java\npublic interface AiProvider {\n    AiSuggestionResult generateSuggestion(AiContext context);\n    boolean isAvailable();\n}\n```\n\nTwo implementations:\n- `OpenRouterAiProvider` — production: calls OpenRouter with per-type prompt templates, rate limiting, token tracking\n- `StubAiProvider` — test/offline: returns realistic canned responses for each suggestion type\n\n### Suggestion Types and Services\n\n| Type | Service | Prompt | Trigger |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `COMMIT_DRAFT_ASSIST` | `CommitDraftAssistService` | `commit-draft-assist.txt` | User clicks \"AI Suggest\" |\n| `COMMIT_LINT` | `CommitLintService` | `commit-lint.txt` | Auto on save + pre-lock |\n| `RCDO_SUGGEST` | `RcdoSuggestService` | `rcdo-suggest.txt` | During commit editing |\n| `RISK_SIGNAL` | `RiskDetectionService` | `risk-signal.txt` | On lock + daily 07:00 UTC |\n| `RECONCILE_ASSIST` | `ReconcileAssistService` | `reconcile-assist.txt` | User clicks \"AI Assist\" |\n| `TEAM_SUMMARY` | `ManagerAiSummaryService` | `team-summary.txt` | On-demand in Team Week |\n| `RAG_INTENT` | `SemanticQueryService` | `rag-intent.txt` | First step of any RAG query |\n| `RAG_QUERY` | `SemanticQueryService` | `rag-query.txt` | Second step — answer synthesis |\n| `TEAM_INSIGHT` | `InsightGenerationService` | `team-insight.txt` | Daily 08:00 UTC + on-demand |\n| `PERSONAL_INSIGHT` | `InsightGenerationService` | `personal-insight.txt` | On lock + daily sweep |\n\n### Risk Detection: Hybrid Rules + LLM\n\n`RiskDetectionService` is the best example of the AI design philosophy — deterministic rules handle what they can, the LLM handles what they can't:\n\n**Rules engine** (always runs, no AI dependency):\n- `OVERCOMMIT` — total points > capacity budget\n- `UNDERCOMMIT` — total points < 60% of budget\n- `REPEATED_CARRY_FORWARD` — any commit with streak ≥ 2\n- `BLOCKED_CRITICAL` — King/Queen linked to blocked ticket > 48 hours\n- `SCOPE_VOLATILITY` — > 3 post-lock scope change events\n\n**LLM augmentation** (runs after rules, degrades gracefully):\n- The prompt explicitly lists the 5 rule-based signals and says \"do NOT duplicate these\"\n- LLM looks for: hidden dependencies, unrealistic estimates, concentration risk, timing conflicts\n- AI-detected signals are stored with separate model version for tracking\n\n### RAG Pipeline Detail\n\n**Indexing (write path):**\n\n```\nEntity event (commit create, lock, reconcile, etc.)\n  → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity()\n    → ChunkBuilder.build*Chunk() with EnrichmentContext\n      (RCDO path, team name, owner, carry-forward lineage,\n       linked ticket summary, cross-team RCDO overlap)\n    → EmbeddingService.embed() (OpenAI text-embedding-3-small)\n    → PineconeClient.upsert() (namespaced by org ID)\n```\n\n**Querying (read path):**\n\n```\nQuestion\n  → Intent classification (LLM: entity types, time range, user scope)\n  → Embed question\n  → Pinecone query (top-40, filtered by team/user/date/entity type)\n  → Context assembly\n  → RAG answer generation (LLM)\n  → Store audit record with source citations\n  → Return answer + sources + confidence\n```\n\n**Chunk enrichment** is critical — raw entity data produces sparse embeddings. The `ChunkBuilder.EnrichmentContext` adds:\n- Full RCDO ancestry path (e.g., \"Rally Cry: Win Enterprise > DO: Improve Uptime > Outcome: 99.9% SLA\")\n- Carry-forward lineage narrative\n- Linked ticket summary with status\n- Cross-team RCDO overlap notes\n- Owner and team context\n\n### Evaluation Infrastructure\n\n**Offline evaluation** (`PromptEvalRunner`, `@Tag(\"eval\")`):\n- Golden test datasets per capability in `backend/src/test/resources/eval/`\n- Calls real LLM with actual prompt templates\n- Automated schema validation + behavioral checks\n- LLM-as-judge scoring (title quality, criteria measurability, faithfulness)\n- 3 runs per case for output variance measurement\n- JSON report output to `build/eval-results/`\n\n**Production evaluation** (`FaithfulnessEvaluator`):\n- Async sampling after suggestion storage\n- 100% of high-stakes types (RISK_SIGNAL, TEAM_INSIGHT, PERSONAL_INSIGHT, RAG_QUERY)\n- 10% of lower-stakes types (COMMIT_DRAFT, COMMIT_LINT)\n- RAGAS-style claim decomposition: faithfulness = supported claims / total claims\n- Scores written back to `ai_suggestion` table\n\n**Observability** (`AiQualityMetrics`):\n- `weekly_commit_ai_faithfulness_score` — rolling 7-day average by suggestion type\n- `weekly_commit_ai_acceptance_rate` — accepted / (accepted + dismissed) by type\n- `weekly_commit_ai_provider_available` — 1/0 gauge\n- `weekly_commit_ai_tokens_total` — cumulative token consumption\n- Prometheus alerts at Manus-recommended thresholds (faithfulness < 0.88 → warning)\n\n### Prompt Version Tracking and A/B Analysis\n\nEvery `ai_suggestion` row stores `prompt_version` (e.g., `commit-draft-assist-v1`). Combined with `ai_feedback` (accept/dismiss), this enables:\n\n```sql\nSELECT prompt_version, suggestion_type,\n       COUNT(*) as total,\n       COUNT(CASE WHEN f.accepted THEN 1 END) as accepted,\n       ROUND(COUNT(CASE WHEN f.accepted THEN 1 END)::decimal\n             / NULLIF(COUNT(f.id), 0), 3) as acceptance_rate\nFROM ai_suggestion s\nLEFT JOIN ai_feedback f ON f.suggestion_id = s.id\nWHERE prompt_version IS NOT NULL\nGROUP BY prompt_version, suggestion_type;\n```\n\n---\n\n## Frontend Architecture\n\n### Micro-Frontend Integration\n\nThe frontend is a Vite-built Module Federation remote:\n\n```typescript\n// Host app loads the remote\nconst WeeklyCommitRoutes = React.lazy(() => import(\"weeklyCommit/Routes\"));\n<WeeklyCommitRoutes bridge={hostBridge} />\n```\n\nThe `HostProvider` injects authenticated user identity, team context, feature flags, and design tokens. For local dev, `MockHostProvider` provides a complete mock bridge with a user-switcher banner.\n\n### Routes\n\n| Route | Page | Primary audience |\n|---|---|---|\n| `/weekly/my-week` | My Week — plan creation, commit list, AI lint, lock | IC |\n| `/weekly/reconcile` | Reconcile — baseline vs actual, outcomes, carry-forward | IC |\n| `/weekly/team` | Team Week — manager dashboard with 6 sections | Manager |\n| `/weekly/tickets` | Tickets — native work item list + detail | All |\n| `/weekly/rcdos` | RCDOs — hierarchy management, archive, move | Manager / Admin |\n| `/weekly/reports` | Reports — compliance, planned vs achieved, RCDO coverage | All |\n| `/weekly/admin` | Admin — org config, cadence settings | Admin |\n\n### AI Components\n\n| Component | Location | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `CommitDraftAssistButton` | Commit form | \"✨ AI Suggest\" with inline diff-style suggestions |\n| `AiLintPanel` | My Week | Commit quality lint with hard vs soft distinction |\n| `RcdoSuggestionInline` | Commit form | RCDO link suggestion with rationale |\n| `RiskSignalsPanel` | My Week | Risk signal display (rules + AI) |\n| `ReconcileAssistPanel` | Reconcile page | AI-assisted outcome suggestions + carry-forward recs |\n| `InsightPanel` | My Week / Team Week | Proactive personal + team insights |\n| `ManagerAiSummaryCard` | Team Week | AI-generated team summary |\n| `SemanticSearchInput` | All pages | Natural-language RAG query input |\n| `QueryAnswerCard` | Search results | RAG answer with source citations |\n| `AiFeedbackButtons` | Every AI output | Thumbs up/down on every suggestion |\n| `AiCommitComposer` | My Week | AI-guided commit creation flow |\n| `ProactiveRiskBanner` | My Week | Banner for critical risk signals |\n| `TeamRiskSummaryBanner` | Team Week | Team-level risk overview |\n\n---\n\n## Observability\n\n### Prometheus Metrics\n- Standard Spring Boot Actuator metrics (HTTP, JVM, HikariCP)\n- Custom AI quality gauges (faithfulness, acceptance rate, provider availability, tokens)\n- Lifecycle job success/failure counters (auto-lock, auto-reconcile)\n\n### Alert Rules (`infra/prometheus/alerts.yml`)\n- `HighErrorRate` — API 5xx > 5% for 2 minutes\n- `SlowEndpoint` — p95 > 2s for 5 minutes\n- `AutoLockJobFailure` / `AutoReconcileJobFailure` — lifecycle job errors\n- `DatabaseConnectionPoolExhausted` — HikariCP > 90%\n- `AiFaithfulnessLow` / `AiFaithfulnessCritical` — AI quality degradation\n- `AiAcceptanceRateLow` — users dismissing > 80% of suggestions\n- `AiProviderDown` — OpenRouter unavailable > 5 minutes\n\n### Structured Logging\n- JSON format via Logstash encoder (production profile)\n- Request tracing across frontend and backend\n- AI suggestion lifecycle logging (request → generate → store → eval → feedback)\n\n---\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n| Layer | Framework | Count | What it covers |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| Backend unit/integration | JUnit 5 + Mockito | 54 test files | Service logic, controller endpoints, AI services, domain validation |\n| Frontend unit | Vitest + Testing Library | 41 test files | Components, hooks, API clients, user flows |\n| E2E | Playwright | 4 spec files | Golden path, AI flows, manager flow, navigation |\n| AI evaluation | Custom eval harness | Golden datasets | Prompt quality, schema validation, LLM-as-judge scoring |\n\n### CI Pipeline\n\nBoth **GitHub Actions** and **GitLab CI** are configured with identical stages:\n\n```\nlint → test-frontend + test-backend → build → e2e → eval (manual, LLM)\n                                                       ↑\n                                                 api-contract (PR only)\n```\n\nThe `eval:llm-judge` stage runs against real LLM APIs and is intentionally manual + `allow_failure` since it depends on external API availability.\n\n---\n\n## Deployment\n\n### Docker Compose\n\n```bash\ndocker compose up --build                           # Core: Postgres, Redis, Backend, Frontend\ndocker compose --profile observability up --build   # + Prometheus + Grafana\n```\n\n### Infrastructure\n\n- `infra/prometheus/` — Prometheus config + alert rules\n- `infra/grafana/provisioning/` — Datasource + dashboard provisioning\n- `infra/terraform/main.tf` — Infrastructure-as-code skeleton\n\n### Environment Variables\n\n| Variable | Required | Purpose |\n|---|---|---|\n| `DB_USER` / `DB_PASSWORD` | Yes | PostgreSQL credentials |\n| `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` | For AI | OpenRouter API key (Claude) |\n| `PINECONE_API_KEY` | For RAG | Pinecone vector database |\n| `OPENAI_API_KEY` | For embeddings | OpenAI embedding model |\n| `APP_SCHEDULING_ENABLED` | No | Enable/disable scheduled jobs (default: true) |\n| `FEATURE_AI_ASSISTANCE` | No | Feature flag for AI (default: true) |\n"

# AI Evaluation & Quality Roadmap

**Created:** 2026-03-26
**Context:** Weekly Commit Module — RAG pipeline uses Pinecone (vector store) + OpenRouter/Claude (LLM) + OpenAI text-embedding-3-small (embeddings). 10 prompt templates, 7 AI service types, 6 frontend AI components. Evaluation gaps identified via code audit and validated against Manus RAG evaluation research report (see `docs/rag-eval-research.md`).

---

## Phase 1: Eval Foundation

**Goal:** Build the infrastructure to scientifically validate AI output quality, enable A/B testing of prompts, and measure the metrics that the Manus research identifies as critical (Faithfulness ≥ 0.90, Context Recall ≥ 0.85).

## Phase 3: Wire Missing Frontend AI Features

**Goal:** Three AI backend capabilities exist but have no frontend component calling them. Wiring these up completes the user-facing AI story.

### 3a. Commit Draft Assist Button in CommitForm

**What:** `CommitDraftAssistService` (backend) and `aiApi.commitDraftAssist()` (frontend API client) exist and work. No UI component calls them.

**Build:** An "✨ AI Suggest" button in the commit creation/edit form that:
1. Calls `aiApi.commitDraftAssist()` with current form values
2. Shows suggestions inline (highlighted diff-style: "Current: X → Suggested: Y")
3. Each suggestion has Accept / Dismiss buttons (using existing `AiFeedbackButtons`)
4. Accepting a suggestion fills the form field
5. Disabled when AI is unavailable (check `useAiStatus()`)

**Location:** New component `frontend/src/components/ai/CommitDraftAssistButton.tsx`, used inside the commit form on the MyWeek page.

**UX notes:**
- Don't auto-run on every keystroke — trigger on explicit button click
- Show loading spinner while waiting
- If all suggestions are null (current values are already good), show "✓ Looks good!"
- Show rationale text in a tooltip or collapsed section

### 3b. Reconcile Assist in ReconcilePage

**What:** `ReconcileAssistService` (backend) exists. No frontend component calls it.

**Build:** An "AI Assist Reconciliation" button on the Reconcile page that:
1. Calls the reconcile assist endpoint with the plan's commits + scope changes
2. Pre-fills likely outcomes (ACHIEVED/PARTIALLY_ACHIEVED/NOT_ACHIEVED/CANCELED) in the `OutcomeSelector` components
3. Shows a draft week summary
4. Suggests which commits to carry forward with reasons
5. All suggestions are editable — user must explicitly accept

**Location:** New component `frontend/src/components/ai/ReconcileAssistPanel.tsx`, used in `frontend/src/routes/Reconcile.tsx`.

### 3c. Suggested Questions in SemanticSearchInput

**What:** When the search input is empty, show 3-4 clickable example questions as pills/chips below the input.

**Build:** Add to `SemanticSearchInput.tsx`:
```tsx
const SUGGESTED_QUESTIONS = [
  "What did the team commit to last week?",
  "Which RCDOs received the most effort this month?",
  "What are the recurring carry-forward patterns?",
  "Which team members are overcommitting?",
];
```

Show these as clickable badges when `question` is empty and no result is displayed. Clicking one fills the input and auto-submits.

---

## Phase 4: Production Monitoring

**Goal:** Continuously validate AI quality in production, detect degradation early, and provide observability into the AI layer's health.

### 4a. Async Eval Sampling

**What:** After each AI suggestion is stored, sample 5-10% and run faithfulness + relevancy scoring asynchronously. Store scores on the `ai_suggestion` row.

**Implementation:**
1. Add columns to `ai_suggestion`: `eval_faithfulness_score REAL`, `eval_relevancy_score REAL`, `eval_scored_at TIMESTAMPTZ`
2. New service: `ProductionEvalService` — after `AiSuggestionService.storeSuggestion()`, probabilistically enqueue an eval job
3. Eval job: call `FaithfulnessEvaluator` (from Phase 1d) + a relevancy judge on the stored suggestion
4. Results written back to the suggestion row

**Sampling strategy:** Score 100% of RISK_SIGNAL and TEAM_INSIGHT suggestions (high-stakes), 10% of COMMIT_DRAFT and COMMIT_LINT (high-volume, lower stakes).

### 4b. Prometheus Metrics for AI Quality

**What:** Expose Prometheus gauges for rolling AI quality metrics. Wire into the existing Grafana setup (provisioning already exists at `infra/grafana/provisioning/`).

**Metrics to expose:**
- `weekly_commit_ai_faithfulness_score` (gauge, labeled by suggestion_type) — rolling 7-day average
- `weekly_commit_ai_acceptance_rate` (gauge, labeled by suggestion_type) — accepted / (accepted + dismissed)
- `weekly_commit_ai_suggestion_latency_seconds` (histogram, labeled by suggestion_type)
- `weekly_commit_ai_provider_availability` (gauge) — 1 if available, 0 if not
- `weekly_commit_ai_total_tokens_used` (counter) — from `OpenRouterAiProvider.getTotalTokensUsed()`

**Grafana dashboard:** Create `infra/grafana/provisioning/dashboards/ai-quality.json` with panels for each metric.

### 4c. Drift Alerting

**What:** Alert when AI quality degrades below Manus-recommended production thresholds.

**Alert rules (add to `infra/prometheus/alerts.yml`):**
- `AiFaithfulnessLow`: rolling 7-day faithfulness < 0.88 → warning
- `AiFaithfulnessCritical`: rolling 7-day faithfulness < 0.85 → critical
- `AiAcceptanceRateLow`: rolling 7-day acceptance rate < 0.20 → warning
- `AiProviderDown`: provider unavailable for > 5 minutes → critical
- `AiLatencyHigh`: p95 suggestion latency > 8 seconds → warning

**Context from Manus report (§8):**
> Production alert thresholds: Faithfulness < 0.88, Context Recall < 0.82, Answer Relevancy < 0.78, P95 Latency > 8s

---

## Reference: Current AI Architecture

```
Write Path (real-time):
  CommitService.create() → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(COMMIT, id)    [async]
  ScopeChangeService.*() → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(SCOPE_CHANGE)  [async]
  CarryForwardService.*() → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(CARRY_FORWARD)[async]
  LockService.lock()     → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(PLAN_SUMMARY)  [async]
                         → InsightGenerationService.generatePersonalInsightsAsync() [async]
  ReconciliationService  → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(PLAN_SUMMARY)  [async]
  ManagerReviewService   → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(MANAGER_COMMENT)[async]
  TicketService.*()      → SemanticIndexService.indexEntity(TICKET)        [async]

Indexing Pipeline:
  Entity → ChunkBuilder.build*Chunk() → EmbeddingService.embed() → PineconeClient.upsert()

Query Pipeline:
  Question → Intent Classification (LLM) → EmbeddingService.embed() → PineconeClient.query()
           → Context Assembly → RAG Answer Generation (LLM) → AiSuggestionService.store()

Scheduled Jobs:
  SemanticIndexService.dailySweepReindex()     — 03:00 UTC, reindexes plans updated in last 48h
  InsightGenerationService.generateDailyInsights() — 08:00 UTC, team + personal insights
  RiskDetectionService.runDailyRiskDetection() — runs on all LOCKED plans

AI Services (10 types):
  COMMIT_DRAFT_ASSIST  → CommitDraftAssistService  → prompt: commit-draft-assist.txt
  COMMIT_LINT          → CommitLintService          → prompt: commit-lint.txt
  RCDO_SUGGEST         → RcdoSuggestService         → prompt: rcdo-suggest.txt
  RISK_SIGNAL          → RiskDetectionService        → prompt: risk-signal.txt (+ rules engine)
  RECONCILE_ASSIST     → ReconcileAssistService      → prompt: reconcile-assist.txt
  TEAM_SUMMARY         → ManagerAiSummaryService     → prompt: team-summary.txt
  RAG_INTENT           → SemanticQueryService        → prompt: rag-intent.txt
  RAG_QUERY            → SemanticQueryService        → prompt: rag-query.txt
  TEAM_INSIGHT         → InsightGenerationService    → prompt: team-insight.txt
  PERSONAL_INSIGHT     → InsightGenerationService    → prompt: personal-insight.txt

Frontend AI Components:
  AiLintPanel            — commit quality lint (calls COMMIT_LINT)
  RiskSignalsPanel       — risk signal display (reads RISK_SIGNAL)
  InsightPanel           — team + personal insights (reads TEAM_INSIGHT, PERSONAL_INSIGHT)
  SemanticSearchInput    — RAG query interface (calls RAG_INTENT + RAG_QUERY)
  QueryAnswerCard        — RAG answer display with source citations
  AiFeedbackButtons      — thumbs up/down on every AI output

  MISSING: CommitDraftAssist UI (backend exists, no frontend component)
  MISSING: ReconcileAssist UI (backend exists, no frontend component)
  MISSING: Suggested questions in SemanticSearchInput
```

## Reference: Key Manus Report Thresholds

| Metric | Dev Gate | Staging Gate | Prod Alert |
|---|---|---|---|
| Faithfulness | ≥ 0.85 | ≥ 0.90 | < 0.88 |
| Context Recall | ≥ 0.80 | ≥ 0.85 | < 0.82 |
| Answer Relevancy | ≥ 0.75 | ≥ 0.80 | < 0.78 |
| Context Precision | ≥ 0.65 | ≥ 0.70 | < 0.68 |
| P95 Latency | < 10s | < 7s | > 8s |
